Primary Propositions vs Propositions with Primary Predicate
Distinguishes primary propositions from those with primary predicate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a primary proposition and a proposition whose predicate is primary, and identify whether a given proposition from Islamic science qualifies as primary.

Core Idea
A primary proposition is self-evident on conception; a proposition with a primary predicate may still need intermediaries.

In the study of demonstration (burhan), it is crucial to know which propositions are truly foundational. The author distinguishes between two types: those that are primary (awwaliyya) and those that have a primary predicate but are not themselves primary. Understanding this difference helps you assess how much justification a proposition already carries.

Guided Path
1
Define 'primary proposition'
According to the passage, a primary proposition has no intermediary between subject and predicate in assent; conception suffices.
Look for the phrase 'ليس بين موضوعها ومحمولها واسطة في التصديق'.
2
Define 'proposition with primary predicate'
Here the predicate is primary (predicated of all things at all times) but the proposition may require intermediaries.
The text says 'كثيرا ما تحتاج إلى وسائط'.
3
Compare the two
Note that the first is self-evident, the second is not necessarily so. The predicate being primary does not make the whole proposition primary.
This distinction is key in the Book of Demonstration.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider the proposition 'The world is temporally originated.' Is its predicate primary? Is the proposition itself primary? Check the text's criteria.
Use the criteria from the passage to decide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه فرق بين أن يقال مقدّمة أولية وبين أن يقال مقدمة محمولها أولي، فإن الأولية هي التي ليس بين موضوعها ومحمولها واسطة في التصديق بل يكفي في التصديق تصورها. وأما الثانية فكثيرا ما تحتاج إلى وسائط والمحمول إنما يكون كليّاً في كتاب البرهان؛ إذ كان مع كونه مقولاً على الكل في كل زمان أوليا، والأعراض الذاتية غير الخاصة بالنوع الذي وجدت له فهي أعراض ذاتية له لأن جنس النوع يؤخذ في حدها، وأعراض ذاتية للجنس لأن الجنس نفسه يؤخذ في حدها. وجنس العرض الذاتي قد يكون عرضًا ذاتيًا لموضوع فقط كالزوج فإنه جنس لزوج الزوج؛ وكل واحد منهما عرض ذاتي للعدد . وقد يكون ذاتياً لا للموضوع فقط بل لجنسه أيضًا نحو المنقسم بمتساويين الذي هو جنس للزوج؛ فإنه ليس عرضًا ذاتيًا فقط لأنه يؤخذ في المقادير أيضًا بل لجنسه الذي هو الكم. والمحمولات الأولية المقومة لماهية الشيء منها ما هي خاصة كالحد وبعض الفصول نحو الحسّاس للحيوان، ومنها ما هي غير خاصة كالجنس وبعض الفصول مثل المنقسم بمتساويين والناطق » إنه مشترك بين الإنسان والملك. ( والجنس أولي غير خاص لأنه لا يحمل على شيء أعم من النوع الذي تحته ثم يحمل على النوع إلا وأن يكون جنسًا متوسطا أو عاليا؛ والحد أولي خاص. وأما المحمولات التي هي أعراض ذاتية فمنها أولية خاصة كحال زوايا المثلث للمثلث، ومنها أولية غير خاصة مثل كون الزاويتين اللتين من جهة واحدة متساويتين لقائمتين فإنه أولي للخط الواقع على خطين المصير زاويتهما المتبادلتين متساويتين. والخط الواقع على خطين المصير زاويتها للخارجة مثل الداخلة ولكن ليس بخاص لأحدهما؛ وهذا الخط وإن كان واحدًا بالذات فهذا بيان بالمعنى وبالاعتبار.
And know that there is a difference between saying a 'primary proposition' and saying a 'proposition whose predicate is primary'. For the primary is that between whose subject and predicate there is no intermediary in assent; rather, in order to assent to it, its conception suffices. As for the second, it often requires intermediaries, and the predicate is only universal in the Book of Demonstration; since, while being predicated of all things at all times, it is primary. And the essential accidents that are not specific to the species for which they exist are essential accidents to it because the genus of the species is taken in its definition; and they are essential accidents to the genus because the genus itself is taken in its definition. And the genus of the essential accident may be an essential accident only to the subject, like 'evenness', for it is a genus for 'evenness of evenness'; and each one of them is an essential accident to number. And it may be essential not only to the subject but also to its genus, like 'divisible into two equal parts' which is a genus for 'evenness'; for it is not only an essential accident because it is taken in quantities as well, but also to its genus which is quantity. And the primary predicates that constitute the quiddity of a thing, among them are specific, like the definition (hadd) and some differentiate (fusul) such as 'sensitive' for animal; and among them are non-specific, like the genus and some differentiate such as 'divisible into two equal parts' and 'rational' — it is common between man and angel. And the genus is primary and non-specific because it is not predicated of anything more general than the species that is under it, then it is predicated of the species except if it is an intermediate or highest genus; and the definition is primary and specific. As for the predicates that are essential accidents, among them are primary and specific, like the state of the angles of a triangle for the triangle; and among them are primary and non-specific, like the fact that the two angles on one side are equal to two right angles, for it is primary for the line falling on two lines such that its alternate angles are equal. And the line falling on two lines such that its exterior angle equals the interior, but it is not specific to either of them; and this line, even though it is one in essence, this is an explanation in meaning and in consideration.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage distinguishes two types of propositions: primary propositions (muqaddima awwaliyya) and propositions whose predicate is primary (muqaddima mahmulaha awwali). The author explains that primary propositions are self-evident upon conception, requiring no intermediary for assent. In contrast, propositions with a primary predicate may require intermediaries, even though the predicate itself is universal and primary in the context of the Book of Demonstration. The discussion then moves to essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyya). Essential accidents that are not specific to a particular species are essential to that species because the genus of the species enters their definition; they are also essential to the genus because the genus itself enters their definition. The author then examines the genus of an essential accident, giving the example of 'evenness' (al-zawj) as a genus for 'evenness of evenness' (zawj al-zawj); both are essential accidents to number. Another example is 'divisible into two equal parts' (al-munqasim bi-mutasawiyayn), which is a genus for 'evenness' and is an essential accident not only to number but also to its own genus, which is quantity (al-kamm). Next, primary predicates are classified. Those that constitute the quiddity (mahiyya) of a thing are either specific (khas) like the definition (hadd) and some differentiate (fusul), or non-specific (ghayr khas) like the genus and some differentiate such as 'divisible into two equal parts' and 'rational' (al-natiq). The author notes that 'rational' is common between humans and angels. The genus is primary and non-specific because it is predicated only of things more specific than itself, except when it is an intermediate or highest genus. The definition is primary and specific. Then, considering predicates that are essential accidents, some are primary and specific, like the property of a triangle's angles summing to two right angles; others are primary but non-specific, like the property of a line intersecting two parallel lines such that alternate angles are equal. The example of the line falling on two lines producing equal exterior and interior angles is given, but this property is not specific to either line alone. The author concludes that although the line is one in essence, the explanation is in meaning and consideration.

Key Terms
مقدمة أولية
مقدمة محمولها أولي

Which of the following best describes a primary proposition according to the passage?
A) A proposition whose predicate is predicated of all things at all times.
B) A proposition in which there is no intermediary between subject and predicate in assent.
C) A proposition that requires intermediaries for assent.
D) A proposition that is used in the Book of Demonstration.

Key Takeaway
A primary proposition is self-evident upon conception, while a proposition with a primary predicate may still require proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the proposition 'Every action of Allah is wise' is a primary proposition or a proposition with a primary predicate according to the criteria in this lesson. Justify your answer using the text.
?
Find a proposition from a kalam text that you think is primary. Then find another that has a primary predicate but is not itself primary. Explain the difference.

Essential Accidents and Classification of Primary Predicates
Classifies essential accidents and primary predicates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify essential accidents based on their genus and distinguish primary predicates that are specific from those that are non-specific, using examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Essential accidents are defined by the genus of their subject; primary predicates are either specific (unique) or non-specific (shared).

Essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyya) are properties that belong to a subject necessarily because their definition includes the subject's genus. The author also categorizes primary predicates (constitutive and accidental) into specific and non-specific. This classification is vital for constructing sound definitions and demonstrations in fields like fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify essential accidents
Find the definition: accidents that are not specific to a species but are essential because the genus of the species enters their definition.
Focus on 'والأعراض الذاتية غير الخاصة بالنوع'.
2
Analyze the genus of an essential accident
Look at examples: evenness is essential to number; its genus (evenness of evenness) is also essential to number. Divisible into two equal parts is essential to number and also to quantity.
This shows how an accident can be essential to multiple levels.
3
Distinguish constitutive vs accidental primary predicates
Constitutive predicates form the quiddity (hadd, fasl). Accidental predicates are essential accidents.
The text lists examples for each.
4
Classify as specific or non-specific
For constitutive: hadd and some fusul are specific; jins and some fusul (e.g., rational shared by human and angel) are non-specific. For accidental: some are specific (triangle's angle sum), some non-specific (properties of parallel lines).
Use the text's criteria: specific = unique to a species; non-specific = shared.
5
Apply to Islamic science examples
Choose a concept from fiqh (e.g., riba) and identify its essential accidents and whether they are specific.
Think about how this classification affects qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه فرق بين أن يقال مقدّمة أولية وبين أن يقال مقدمة محمولها أولي، فإن الأولية هي التي ليس بين موضوعها ومحمولها واسطة في التصديق بل يكفي في التصديق تصورها. وأما الثانية فكثيرا ما تحتاج إلى وسائط والمحمول إنما يكون كليّاً في كتاب البرهان؛ إذ كان مع كونه مقولاً على الكل في كل زمان أوليا، والأعراض الذاتية غير الخاصة بالنوع الذي وجدت له فهي أعراض ذاتية له لأن جنس النوع يؤخذ في حدها، وأعراض ذاتية للجنس لأن الجنس نفسه يؤخذ في حدها. وجنس العرض الذاتي قد يكون عرضًا ذاتيًا لموضوع فقط كالزوج فإنه جنس لزوج الزوج؛ وكل واحد منهما عرض ذاتي للعدد . وقد يكون ذاتياً لا للموضوع فقط بل لجنسه أيضًا نحو المنقسم بمتساويين الذي هو جنس للزوج؛ فإنه ليس عرضًا ذاتيًا فقط لأنه يؤخذ في المقادير أيضًا بل لجنسه الذي هو الكم. والمحمولات الأولية المقومة لماهية الشيء منها ما هي خاصة كالحد وبعض الفصول نحو الحسّاس للحيوان، ومنها ما هي غير خاصة كالجنس وبعض الفصول مثل المنقسم بمتساويين والناطق » إنه مشترك بين الإنسان والملك. ( والجنس أولي غير خاص لأنه لا يحمل على شيء أعم من النوع الذي تحته ثم يحمل على النوع إلا وأن يكون جنسًا متوسطا أو عاليا؛ والحد أولي خاص. وأما المحمولات التي هي أعراض ذاتية فمنها أولية خاصة كحال زوايا المثلث للمثلث، ومنها أولية غير خاصة مثل كون الزاويتين اللتين من جهة واحدة متساويتين لقائمتين فإنه أولي للخط الواقع على خطين المصير زاويتهما المتبادلتين متساويتين. والخط الواقع على خطين المصير زاويتها للخارجة مثل الداخلة ولكن ليس بخاص لأحدهما؛ وهذا الخط وإن كان واحدًا بالذات فهذا بيان بالمعنى وبالاعتبار.
And know that there is a difference between saying a 'primary proposition' and saying a 'proposition whose predicate is primary'. For the primary is that between whose subject and predicate there is no intermediary in assent; rather, in order to assent to it, its conception suffices. As for the second, it often requires intermediaries, and the predicate is only universal in the Book of Demonstration; since, while being predicated of all things at all times, it is primary. And the essential accidents that are not specific to the species for which they exist are essential accidents to it because the genus of the species is taken in its definition; and they are essential accidents to the genus because the genus itself is taken in its definition. And the genus of the essential accident may be an essential accident only to the subject, like 'evenness', for it is a genus for 'evenness of evenness'; and each one of them is an essential accident to number. And it may be essential not only to the subject but also to its genus, like 'divisible into two equal parts' which is a genus for 'evenness'; for it is not only an essential accident because it is taken in quantities as well, but also to its genus which is quantity. And the primary predicates that constitute the quiddity of a thing, among them are specific, like the definition (hadd) and some differentiate (fusul) such as 'sensitive' for animal; and among them are non-specific, like the genus and some differentiate such as 'divisible into two equal parts' and 'rational' — it is common between man and angel. And the genus is primary and non-specific because it is not predicated of anything more general than the species that is under it, then it is predicated of the species except if it is an intermediate or highest genus; and the definition is primary and specific. As for the predicates that are essential accidents, among them are primary and specific, like the state of the angles of a triangle for the triangle; and among them are primary and non-specific, like the fact that the two angles on one side are equal to two right angles, for it is primary for the line falling on two lines such that its alternate angles are equal. And the line falling on two lines such that its exterior angle equals the interior, but it is not specific to either of them; and this line, even though it is one in essence, this is an explanation in meaning and in consideration.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage distinguishes two types of propositions: primary propositions (muqaddima awwaliyya) and propositions whose predicate is primary (muqaddima mahmulaha awwali). The author explains that primary propositions are self-evident upon conception, requiring no intermediary for assent. In contrast, propositions with a primary predicate may require intermediaries, even though the predicate itself is universal and primary in the context of the Book of Demonstration. The discussion then moves to essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyya). Essential accidents that are not specific to a particular species are essential to that species because the genus of the species enters their definition; they are also essential to the genus because the genus itself enters their definition. The author then examines the genus of an essential accident, giving the example of 'evenness' (al-zawj) as a genus for 'evenness of evenness' (zawj al-zawj); both are essential accidents to number. Another example is 'divisible into two equal parts' (al-munqasim bi-mutasawiyayn), which is a genus for 'evenness' and is an essential accident not only to number but also to its own genus, which is quantity (al-kamm). Next, primary predicates are classified. Those that constitute the quiddity (mahiyya) of a thing are either specific (khas) like the definition (hadd) and some differentiate (fusul), or non-specific (ghayr khas) like the genus and some differentiate such as 'divisible into two equal parts' and 'rational' (al-natiq). The author notes that 'rational' is common between humans and angels. The genus is primary and non-specific because it is predicated only of things more specific than itself, except when it is an intermediate or highest genus. The definition is primary and specific. Then, considering predicates that are essential accidents, some are primary and specific, like the property of a triangle's angles summing to two right angles; others are primary but non-specific, like the property of a line intersecting two parallel lines such that alternate angles are equal. The example of the line falling on two lines producing equal exterior and interior angles is given, but this property is not specific to either line alone. The author concludes that although the line is one in essence, the explanation is in meaning and consideration.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتي
محمول أولي خاص
محمول أولي غير خاص

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a primary predicate that is non-specific?
A) The definition (hadd) of a thing
B) The genus (jins)
C) The state of a triangle's angles summing to two right angles
D) The property of being sensitive for an animal

Key Takeaway
Essential accidents are defined by the subject's genus, and primary predicates are classified as specific (unique) or non-specific (shared), with examples from geometry and metaphysics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
